window.acrAsinHover
=
e;








else
if(window.acrAsinHover
==
e)

=
null;






}



amznJQ.onReady('popover',
function()
{




(function($)
{






if($.fn.acrPopover)
return;






var
popoverConfig
=
{








showOnHover:true,








showCloseButton:
true,








width:
null,








location:'bottom',








locationAlign:'left',








locationOffset:[-20,0],








paddingLeft:
15,








paddingBottom:
5,








paddingRight:
15,








group:
'reviewsPopover',








clone:false,








hoverHideDelay:300






};







$.fn.acrPopover
=
function()
{










return
this.each(function()
{












var
$this
=
$(this);












if(!$this.data('init')
&&
typeof
$this.amazonPopoverTrigger
===
'function')
{














$this.data('init',
1);














var
getargs
=
$this.attr('getargs');














var
ajaxURL
=
'/gp/customer-reviews/common/du/displayHistoPopAjax.html?'
+

























'&ASIN='
+
$this.attr('name')
+

























'&link=1'
+

























'&seeall=1'
+

























'&ref='
+
$this.attr('ref')
+

























((typeof
getargs
!=
'undefined')
?
('&getargs='
+
getargs)
:
'');














var
myConfig
=
$.extend(true,
{
destination:
ajaxURL
},
popoverConfig);














$this.amazonPopoverTrigger(myConfig);















var
w
=
window.acrAsinHover;














if(w
&&
$(w).parents('.asinReviewsSummary').get(0)
==
this)
{
















$this.trigger('mouseover.amzPopover');
















window.acrAsinHover
=
null;














}












}








});






};







window.reviewHistPopoverConfig
=
popoverConfig;






var
jqInit
=
window.jQueryInitHistoPopovers
=
function(asin)
{








if
(typeof
$('.acr-popover[name='
+
asin
+
']').acrPopover
===
'function')
{

+
asin
+
']').acrPopover();








}






};






window.doInit_average_customer_reviews
=
jqInit;






window.onAjaxUpdate_average_customer_reviews
=
jqInit;






window.onCacheUpdate_average_customer_reviews
=
jqInit;






window.onCacheUpdateReselect_average_customer_reviews
=
jqInit;







amznJQ.onCompletion('amznJQ.criticalFeature',
function()
{










setTimeout(function()
{
amznJQ.declareAvailable('acrPopover');
},
10);






});




})(jQuery);


});

<span

<a
href="http://www.amazon.com/review/R1HW6CYNG7YD23/ref=cm_cr_dp_title/189-5681517-6267739?ie=UTF8&amp;ASIN=B000002MGR&amp;nodeID=5174&amp;store=music"
class="txtlarge
gl3
gr4
reviewTitle
valignMiddle"><strong>Let
It
Snow</strong></a>











<span
class="gry
valignMiddle">
<span
class="inlineblock
txtsmall">July
26,
2005</span>
</span>










</div>











<div
class="mt4
ath">











<span
class="gr10">
<span
class="txtsmall"><span
class="gry">By</span>
<a
href="/gp/pdp/profile/A3W0R2BLZ0FK3O/ref=cm_cr_dp_pdp/189-5681517-6267739"
class="noTextDecoration">H.
Walsh</a></span>
</span>

<div
class="txtsmall
mt4
fvavp">











<span
class="inlineblock
formatVariation"><span
class="gr3
gry
formatKey">Format:</span><span
class="formatValue">Audio
CD</span></span>










</div>











<div
class="mt9
reviewText">












<div
class="drkgry">













This
is
probably
my
favorite
early
80's
so
called
&quot;New
Wave&quot;
album.
I
wouldn't
even
put
this
album
in
the
New
Wave
or
any
other
category,
because
I
believe
it
shows
a
truly
original
creativity
that
transcends
any
genre.
This
record
creates
an
&quot;atmosphere&quot;
that
takes
the
listener
on
a
beautiful
trip.
I
would
compare
it
to
a
walk
with
your
lover
on
a
wonderful
fall
day
in
an
English
garden;
you
never
tire
of
the
feeling
it
gives.
Personal
favorites
include
&quot;Someone's
Calling&quot;
and
&quot;Face
of
Wood,&quot;
but
all
the
songs
flow
together
as
if
being
played
in
a
suite.
I
think
the
entire
album
shows
wonderful
attention
to
detail
in
both
lyrics
and
musicianship.
In
an
era
where
a
band's
looks
in
it's
videos
were
the
most
important
element,
Modern
English
threw
that
concept
out
the
window
and
contributed
an
artisitc
statement
and
musical
feel
that
few
bands
from
that
era
could
capture.
Ever
notice
how
a
winter
snowfall
brings
beauty
to
everything
it
covers?
&quot;After
the
Snow&quot;
will
add
beauty
and
wonder
to
your
CD
collection.












</div>











</div>

class="clearboth
txtsmall

<div
class="clearboth"></div>











<div
class="mt4
ttl">











<span
class="swSprite
s_star_4_0
"
title="4.0
out
of
5
stars"><span>4.0
out
of
5
stars</span></span>












<a
href="http://www.amazon.com/review/RBAZ16Y8DBYVB/ref=cm_cr_dp_title/189-5681517-6267739?ie=UTF8&amp;ASIN=B000002MGR&amp;nodeID=5174&amp;store=music"
class="txtlarge
gl3
gr4
reviewTitle
valignMiddle"><strong>Pleasant,
underrated
'80s
New
Wave.</strong></a>











<span
class="gry
valignMiddle">
<span
class="inlineblock
txtsmall">August
30,
1999</span>
</span>










</div>











<div
class="mt4
ath">











<span
class="gr10">
<span
class="txtsmall"><span
class="gry">By</span>
A
Customer</span>
</span>











</div>











<div
class="txtsmall
mt4
fvavp">











<span
class="inlineblock
formatVariation"><span
class="gr3
gry
formatKey">Format:</span><span
class="formatValue">Audio
CD</span></span>










</div>











<div
class="mt9
reviewText">












<div
class="drkgry">













<span
class="MHRHead">After
the
Snow
is
truly
an
expression
of
Eighties
music
at
its
near-best.
In
addition
to
the
euphoric
and
well-known
&quot;I
Melt
With
You,&quot;
After
the
Snow
contains
7
other
(mostly)
great
songs,
as
well
as
5
bonus
tracks.
What
we
find
here
is
rich
'80s
New
Wave
rock,
held
together
by
a
gentle,
distinctly
folky
mellowness
(&quot;Carry
Me
Down&quot;
even
features
a
trilling
flute
and
a
gentle
acoustic
guitar)
that's
just
British
enough
to
be
umistakeably
a
gem
of
an
era
gone
for
nearly
15
years,
and
to
resemble
The
Cure's
less
depressing
times.
This
calm
sound,
parallel
with
Robbie
Grey's
clear,
deadpan
English
vocals
is
decorated
sparsely
with
thin,
jerky
guitars
worthy
of
early
Siouxsie
and
the
Banshees
or
U2.
The
two
contrasting
styles
compliment
each
other
quite
nicely,
and
are
punctuated
occasionally
by
Stephen
Walker's
bubbly,
robotic
keyboards,
which
sound
as
if
they
remain
buried
in
the
mix
for
most
of
each
song
and
are
only
allowed
to
come
up
for
air
every
once
in
a
while.
These
keyboards
can
sound
typically
and
humorously
'80s,
but
overall
they
do
not
detract
from
the
soung.
The
songs,
conveniently
helped
along
by
their
folkiness,
mostly
center
on
reflection
and
often
the
beauty
of
nature,
but
at
times
can
escalate
into
tense,
dark
cynicism,
as
as
in
the
dark
reminsicience
of
&quot;After
the
Snow&quot;.
These
explosions
have
more
in
common
with
the
darker,
'80s
Goth
bands;
unexpected
in
light
of
the
more
optimistic
tone
of
this
CD,
but
not
totally
mysterious,
since
After
the
Snow
was
released
on
4AD,
the
division
of
Beggar's
Banquet,
which
has
been
home
to
such
Goth
greats
as
Bauhaus,
Love
and
Rockets,
The
Birthday
Party,
Gary
Numan
and
The
Cult.</span>












<span
class="MHRRest"
style="display:none">
While
delineating
each
aspect
of
this
music
may
make
each
one
sound
clashing
or
egregious
they
blend
together
very
harmoniously.
This
album
may
be
too
calm
or
bland
for
some,
but
I
highly
recommend
it
to
fans
of
New
Wave
or
other
'80s
styles,
and
younger
fans
raised
on
more
recent
Alternative
Rock
may
find
something
relaxing
and
pleasant
here.</span>













<a
href="http://www.amazon.com/After-Snow-Modern-English/product-reviews/B000002MGR/ref=cm_cr_dp_text/189-5681517-6267739?ie=UTF8&amp;showViewpoints=0&amp;sortBy=byRankDescending#RBAZ16Y8DBYVB"
class="MHRExpandLink
readMoreLink">Read
more
&#8250;</a>












</div>

<div

class="reviews"

<div
class="gry

hlp">











4
of
4

found
the

review
helpful










</div>











<div
class="clearboth"></div>











<div
class="mt4
ttl">











<span
class="swSprite
s_star_4_0
"
title="4.0
out
of
5
stars"><span>4.0
out
of
5
stars</span></span>












<a
href="http://www.amazon.com/review/R2OL2QUXP99WD0/ref=cm_cr_dp_title/189-5681517-6267739?ie=UTF8&amp;ASIN=B000002MGR&amp;nodeID=5174&amp;store=music"
class="txtlarge
gl3
gr4
reviewTitle
valignMiddle"><strong>More
than
&quot;Melt
With
You&quot;</strong></a>











<span
class="gry
valignMiddle">
<span
class="inlineblock
txtsmall">November
14,
2006</span>
</span>










</div>











<div
class="mt4
ath">











<span
class="gr10">
<span
class="txtsmall"><span
class="gry">By</span>
<a
href="/gp/pdp/profile/A1TI60NGQSD762/ref=cm_cr_dp_pdp/189-5681517-6267739"
class="noTextDecoration">WalterDigsTunes</a></span>
</span>











</div>











<div
class="txtsmall
mt4
fvavp">











<span
class="inlineblock
formatVariation"><span
class="gr3
gry
formatKey">Format:</span><span
class="formatValue">Audio
CD</span></span>










</div>











<div
class="mt9
reviewText">












<div
class="drkgry">













&quot;Melt
With
You&quot;
is
synonymous
with
an
era,
no
doubt
about
it.
But
should
the
album
whence
it
sprang
be
relegated
to
oblivion?












<br
/>












<br
/>I
think
not.
While
&quot;Melt
With
You&quot;
might
be
early-80s
pop
of
the
moodiest
and
most
perversely
populist
sort,
the
rest
of
the
album
is
imbued
with
a
personality
of
its
own.
&quot;Life
in
the
Gladhouse&quot;
is
a
stomping
beast
that
gallops
along
to
its
own
beat.
&quot;Dawn
Chorus&quot;
and
&quot;Face
of
Wood&quot;
all
have
elements
that
linger
in
the
recesses
of
memory.
&quot;Carry
Me
Down&quot;
is
almost
wistfully
medieval
in
its
execution,
yet
not
in
a
pretentious
proggy
way.
For
the
most
part,
the
album's
production
aptly
presents
the
music
in
a
competent
manner.












<br
/>












<br
/>The
bonus
tracks
that
are
tacked
on
the
back
of
this
re-issue
are
rather
cumbersome,
since
most
are
demos
and
alternate
takes.
&quot;The
Choiciest
View&quot;
is
an
interesting
addition,
since
it
somehow
degenerates
into
self-indulgent
feedback
shenanigans
of
the
most
V.U.-esque
quality.












<br
/>












<br
/>Overall,
this
is
worth
checking
out
if
you're
a
fan
of
post-punk
bands.
Synth-pop
this
isn't,
mind
you,
and
neither
is
it
sparse
Gang
of
Four/Public
Image
Ltd.-circa
1979
stuff.
It's
more
along
the
lines
of
a
less
austere
Joy
Division
having
a
crack
at
fun.












<br
/>












<br
/>Final
verdict:
Recommended.












</div>











</div>

txtsmall

vtStripe">

<a

class="txtlarge
gl3
gr4
reviewTitle
valignMiddle"><strong>Contains
one
of
the
greatest
songs
ever</strong></a>











<span
class="gry
valignMiddle">
<span
class="inlineblock
txtsmall">July
30,
2007</span>
</span>










</div>











<div
class="mt4
ath">











<span
class="gr10">
<span
class="txtsmall"><span
class="gry">By</span>
<a
href="/gp/pdp/profile/A1SLVQKERJUS16/ref=cm_cr_dp_pdp/189-5681517-6267739"
class="noTextDecoration">Mike
Smith</a></span>
</span>











</div>











<div
class="txtsmall
mt4
fvavp">











<span
class="inlineblock
formatVariation"><span
class="gr3
gry
formatKey">Format:</span><span
class="formatValue">Audio
CD</span></span>










</div>











<div
class="mt9
reviewText">












<div
class="drkgry">













There
is
definitely
more
than
one
great
song
on
this
album,
definitely,
but
one
of
those
songs
is
so
great,
so
catchy,
and
so
original
that
all
the
other
songs
can't
help
but
look
a
little
paler
when
placed
next
to
it.












<br
/>&quot;I'll
Melt
With
You&quot;
has
seriously
got
to
be
one
of
the
best
songs
ever--the
&quot;Don't
Fear
the
Reaper&quot;
of
1980s
New
Wave--epic,
anthemic,
wildly
structured,
feel-good,
and
evidently
made
for
driving
and
singing
along.
What
a
song!
What
a
song.












<br
/>&quot;I'll
Melt
With
You&quot;
is
a
song
that
simaltaneously
defines
and
transcends
the
1980s--the
wildness
of
an
effeminately
dressed
and
coifed
rebellion,
the
happiness
of
smiling
hooligans,
the
sort
of
time
when
everyone
(everyone
white
and
middle
class
and
American,
anyway)
seemed
to
say
&quot;That's
cool&quot;
instead
of
&quot;That
sucks.&quot;












<br
/>I
lived
through
it
as
a
kid,
and
I'm
still
living
through
it
through
my
older
brothers
and
through
music
such
as
this.












<br
/>&quot;I'll
Melt
With
You&quot;
is
almost
enough
to
make
this
a
five-star
album,
and
maybe
it
is
enough.
The
other
seven
songs
are
generally
catchy
as
well,
if
a
bit
Duran
Duran-esque
and
a
bit
dated.
They
haven't
aged
quite
as
well
as
most
of
The
Smiths'
songs.












<br
/>If
I
were
to
make
a
mix
tape
with
one
or
two
songs
for
every
decade,
I'd
probably
have
&quot;I'll
Melt
With
You&quot;
represent
the
'80s.
It
deserves
its
reputation
as
a
classic,
and
this
album,
&quot;After
the
Snow,&quot;
deserves
a
good
listen.












</div>











</div>
